#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####

#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)

#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.

#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.

I understand. We need to implement a chess queen attack detector. Let's think through this carefully.

Since the problem involves positions on a chessboard, we need to represent the positions of the queens and check if they can attack each other. The queens can attack if they are on the same row, same column, or same diagonal.

First, we need to parse the positions which are given in chess notation (like 'a1', 'h8', etc.). Chess notation uses:
- Columns: 'a' to 'h' (which map to 0-7)
- Rows: '1' to '8' (which map to 0-7)

However, in the example, 'c5' is at column 2, row 3, which suggests:
- 'c' is the 3rd letter, but index 2 (0-based)
- '5' is the 5th number, but index 3 (0-based) which suggests rows are numbered from the bottom

Wait, but the implementation needs to be consistent. Let's implement a class to hold the positions and check for attacks.

1. Create a class to represent a queen's position
2. Implement a function to check if two queens can attack each other

Now for the implementation in queen_attack.cpp:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if ((white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == (white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    if ((white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == (black_pos.second - white_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Wait, the differences can be negative, so using signed types makes sense
Since the maximum difference is 7-0=7 or 0-7=-7, which fits in int8_t

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if ((white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == (white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    if ((white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == (black_pos.second - white_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // To avoid using abs(), we can compare the squares
    const std::int8_t dx = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    const std::int8_t dy = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    // Since dx and dy could be negative, we need to compare their absolute values
    // But to avoid using abs(), we can square them or compare in a different way
    // For an 8x8 board, this is fine
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (std::int8_t i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (std::int8_t j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation now uses fixed-width integer types and properly handles the diagonal check by comparing dx and dy directly. Since the differences can be positive or negative, we check if dx equals dy or dx equals -dy to cover both diagonal directions.

Note: The loop variables `i` and `j` are now declared as `std::int8_t` to be consistent with the position types. Since they range from 0 to 7, which fits within the range of `std::int8_t` (which can hold up to 127), this is safe.

I understand. The issue is that we need to ensure all integer types are appropriate and follow the MISRA C++ rules. Since the positions on a chessboard are always non-negative (0-7), we should use unsigned types. Let's use `std::uint8_t` instead.

However, when we compute differences, they could be negative, so we need to be careful. Let's cast to signed types when doing subtraction to avoid underflow issues.

Now for the implementation file, we need to adjust the types and handle the differences correctly:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // To avoid using abs(), we can compare the squares
    const std::int8_t dx = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    const std::int8_t dy = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    // Since dx and dy could be negative, we need to compare their absolute values
    // But to avoid using abs(), we can square them or compare in a different way
    // For an 8x8 board, this is fine
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (std::int8_t i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (std::int8_t j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white, std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    // Cast to int to avoid underflow when subtracting
    const int dx = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int dy = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (std::uint8_t i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (std::uint8_t j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation now uses `std::uint8_t` for positions, which is more appropriate since positions can't be negative. When computing differences, we cast to `int` to ensure we can handle negative values correctly. This follows the MISRA C++ rules by being explicit about our types and conversions.

```cpp
=======
bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    // Cast to int to avoid underflow when subtracting
    const int dx = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int dy = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal using multiplication to avoid abs()
    // To follow parentheses rules, we'll wrap each comparison
    if ((dx == dy) || (dx == -dy)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
```

This follows the rule to parenthesize each relational test before combining with ||

I understand the issue. The test is expecting `std::pair<int, int>` but our implementation uses `std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t>`. Let's fix this by changing our implementation to use `int` types instead, which will match the test's expectations.

Here are the necessary changes:

queen_attack.h

```cpp
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> white, std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::uint8_t, std::uint8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    // Cast to int to avoid underflow when subtracting
    const int dx = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int dy = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal using multiplication to avoid abs()
    // To follow parentheses rules, we'll wrap each comparison
    if ((dx == dy) || (dx == -dy)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (std::uint8_t i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (std::uint8_t j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======

        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

    return white_pos;
}

    return black_pos;

    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    const int dx = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    const int dy = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

    std::stringstream board;

            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {

                board << 'B';

                board << '_';
```

I understand. The implementation needs to follow the MISRA C++ rules, which means we need to use fixed-width integer types instead of plain `int`. However, the tests expect `std::pair<int, int>`, so we need to find a way to satisfy both requirements.

Since the tests are fixed and can't be changed, we need to ensure our implementation uses fixed-width types internally but converts to `int` when interfacing with the tests. Let's use `std::int8_t` internally and cast when necessary.

Here are the necessary changes:

```cpp
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }

=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(0), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(7), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(white.first), 
                               static_cast<std::int8_t>(white.second))),
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(black.first), 
                               static_cast<std::int8_t>(black.second))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first), 
                          static_cast<int>(white_pos.second));
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(black_pos.first), 
                          static_cast<int>(black_pos.second));
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    // Cast to int to ensure proper signed arithmetic
    const int dx = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int dy = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            // Compare using the internal int8_t types
            if ((static_cast<std::int8_t>(i) == white_pos.first) && 
                (static_cast<std::int8_t>(j) == white_pos.second)) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if ((static_cast<std::int8_t>(i) == black_pos.first) && 
                       (static_cast<std::int8_t>(j) == black_pos.second)) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(0, 3)), black_pos(std::make_pair(7, 3)) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    const int dx = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    const int dy = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            if (std::make_pair(i, j) == white_pos) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if (std::make_pair(i, j) == black_pos) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <sstream>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <utility>
#include <cctype>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board() 
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(0), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))), 
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(7), static_cast<std::int8_t>(3))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black)
    : white_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(white.first), 
                               static_cast<std::int8_t>(white.second))),
      black_pos(std::make_pair(static_cast<std::int8_t>(black.first), 
                               static_cast<std::int8_t>(black.second))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first), 
                          static_cast<int>(white_pos.second));
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return std::make_pair(static_cast<int>(black_pos.first), 
                          static_cast<int>(black_pos.second));
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal by comparing absolute differences
    // Cast to int to ensure proper signed arithmetic
    const int dx = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    const int dy = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    // Check if the absolute differences are equal
    if (dx == dy) {
        return true;
    }
    if (dx == -dy) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

chess_board::operator std::string() const {
    std::stringstream board;
    for (int i = 0; i < 8; i++) {
        for (int j = 0; j < 8; j++) {
            // Compare using the internal int8_t types
            if ((static_cast<std::int8_t>(i) == white_pos.first) && 
                (static_cast<std::int8_t>(j) == white_pos.second)) {
                board << 'W';
            } else if ((static_cast<std::int8_t>(i) == black_pos.first) && 
                       (static_cast<std::int8_t>(j) == black_pos.second)) {
                board << 'B';
            } else {
                board << '_';
            }
            if (j < 7) {
                board << ' ';
            }
        }
        board << '\n';
    }
    return board.str();
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
